There\\n11: /// is no \\\"pass\\\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\\n18: /// single ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\\n65: \\n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\\n67: /// passes.\\n68: ///\\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\\n72:   static StringRef name() {\\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n74:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\\n76:     Name.consume_front(\\\"llvm::\\\");\\n77:     return Name;\\n78:   }\\n79: \\n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\\n84:     OS << PassName;\\n85:   }\\n86: };\\n87: \\n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\\n89: ///\\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\n95:   ///\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\n99:   ///\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\c AnalysisKey\\n101:   /// member called \\\\c Key.\\n102:   ///\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n111:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\\n113:   }\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: namespace detail {\\n117: \\n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\\n121:           typename... ArgTs, size_t... It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\\n202:   }\\n203: \\n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\\n209:   template Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\\n214:   }\\n215: \\n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\\n218: \\n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\\n220: \\n221: protected:\\n222:   using PassConceptT =\\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n224: \\n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\\n226: };\\n227: \\n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\\n230: \\n231: module provided.\\n19: ///\\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\\n21: /// modules and functions.\\n22: ///\\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\\n24: ///   a Function.\\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\\n26: ///\\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \\\"Value Semantics and Concept-based\\n29: /// Polymorphism\\\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \\\"Inheritance Is The Base\\n30: /// Class of Evil\\\") by Sean Parent:\\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\\n33: /// * ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\\n65: \\n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\\n67: /// passes.\\n68: ///\\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\\n72:   static StringRef name() {\\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n74:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\\n76:     Name.consume_front(\\\"llvm::\\\");\\n77:     return Name;\\n78:   }\\n79: \\n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\\n84:     OS << PassName;\\n85:   }\\n86: };\\n87: \\n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\\n89: ///\\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\n95:   ///\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\n99:   ///\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\c AnalysisKey\\n101:   /// member called \\\\c Key.\\n102:   ///\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n111:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\\n113:   }\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: namespace detail {\\n117: \\n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\\n121:           typename... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\\n202:   }\\n203: \\n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. It is suitable to run\\n196:   /// repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy important\\n197:   /// information about the semantics of the IR.\\n198:   ///\\n199:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. It does, however, perform inlining and other\\n215:   /// heuristic based simplifications that are not strictly reversible.\\n216:   ///\\n217:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. It includes vectorization and other information destroying\\n241:   /// transformations. It works to minimize the IR which needs to be analyzed without\\n295:   /// making irreversible decisions which could be made better during the LTO\\n296:   /// run.\\n297:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n298:   buildLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level);\\n299: \\n300:   /// Build an LTO default optimization pipeline to a pass manager.\\n301:   ///\\n302:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for link-time\\n303:   /// optimization and code generation. It is particularly tuned to fit well\\n304:   /// when IR coming into the LTO phase was first run through \\\\c\\n305:   /// buildLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline, and the two coordinate closely.\\n306:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildLTODefaultPipeline(\\n307:       OptimizationLevel Level, ModuleSummaryIndex *ExportSummary);\\n308: \\n309:   /// Build an O0 pipeline with the minimal semantically required passes.\\n310:   ///\\n311:   /// This should only be used for non-LTO and LTO pre-link pipelines.\\n312:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n313:   buildO0DefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\\n314:                          ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase = ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None);\\n315: \\n316:   /// Build the default `AAManager` with the default alias analysis pipeline\\n317:   /// registered.\\n318:   ///\\n319:   /// This also adds target-specific alias analyses registered via\\n320:   /// TargetMachine::registerDefaultAliasAnalyses().\\n321:   LLVM_ABI AAManager buildDefaultAAPipeline();\\n322: \\n323:   /// Parse a textual pass pipeline description into a \\\\c\\n324:   /// ModulePassManager.\\n325:   ///\\n326:   /// The format of the textual pass pipeline description looks something like:\\n327:   ///\\n328:   ///   module(function(instcombine,sroa),dce,cgscc(inliner,function(...)),...)\\n329:   ///\\n330:   /// Pass managers have ()s describing the nest structure of passes. All passes\\n331:   /// are comma separated. As a special shortcut, if the very first pass is not\\n332:   /// a module pass (as a module pass manager is), this will automatically form\\n333:   /// the shortest stack of pass managers that allow inserting that first pass.\\n334:   /// So, assuming function passes 'fpassN', CGSCC passes 'cgpassN', and loop\\n335:   /// passes 'lpassN', all of these are valid:\\n336:   ///\\n337:   /// If the\\n127:   /// name is the name of a pass, the InnerPipeline is empty, since passes\\n128:   /// cannot contain inner pipelines. See parsePassPipeline() for a more\\n129:   /// detailed description of the textual pipeline format.\\n130:   struct PipelineElement {\\n131:     StringRef Name;\\n132:     std::vector<PipelineElement> InnerPipeline;\\n133:   };\\n134: \\n135:   LLVM_ABI explicit PassBuilder(\\n136:       TargetMachine *TM = nullptr,\\n137:       PipelineTuningOptions PTO = PipelineTuningOptions(),\\n138:       std::optional<PGOOptions> PGOOpt = std::nullopt,\\n139:       PassInstrumentationCallbacks *PIC = nullptr,\\n140:       IntrusiveRefCntPtr<vfs::FileSystem> FS = vfs::getRealFileSystem());\\n141: \\n142:   /// Cross register the analysis managers through their proxies.\\n143:   ///\\n144:   /// This is an interface that can be used to cross register each\\n145:   /// AnalysisManager with all the others analysis managers.\\n146:   LLVM_ABI void\\n147:   crossRegisterProxies(LoopAnalysisManager &LAM, FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM,\\n148:                        CGSCCAnalysisManager &CGAM, ModuleAnalysisManager &MAM,\\n149:                        MachineFunctionAnalysisManager *MFAM = nullptr);\\n150: \\n151:   /// Registers all available module analysis passes.\\n152:   ///\\n153:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c\\n154:   /// ModuleAnalysisManager with all registered module analyses. Callers can\\n155:   /// still manually register any additional analyses. Callers can also\\n156:   /// pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\\n157:   LLVM_ABI void registerModuleAnalyses(ModuleAnalysisManager &MAM);\\n158: \\n159:   /// Registers all available CGSCC analysis passes.\\n160:   ///\\n161:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c CGSCCAnalysisManager\\n162:   /// with all registered CGSCC analyses. Callers can still manually register any\\n163:   /// additional analyses. Callers can also pre-register analyses and this will\\n164:   /// not override those.\\n165:   LLVM_ABI void registerCGSCCAnalyses(CGSCCAnalysisManager &CGAM);\\n166: \\n167:   /// Registers all available function analysis passes.\\n168:   ///\\n169:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c\\n170:   /// FunctionAnalysisManager with all registered function analyses. Callers can\\n171:   /// still manually register any additional analyses. Callers can also\\n172:   /// pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\\n173:   LLVM_ABI void registerFunctionAnalyses(FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM);\\n174: \\n175:   /// Registers all available loop analysis passes.\\n176:   ///\\n177:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c LoopAnalysisManager\\n178:   /// with all registered loop analyses. Callers can still manually register any\\n179:   /// additional analyses.\\n180:   LLVM_ABI void registerLoopAnalyses(LoopAnalysisManager &LAM);\\n181: \\n182:   /// Registers all available machine function analysis passes.\\n183:   ///\\n184:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\\\c\\n185:   /// MachineFunctionAnalysisManager with all registered function analyses.\\n186:   /// Callers can still manually register any additional analyses. Callers can\\n187:   /// also pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\\n188:   LLVM_ABI void\\n189:   registerMachineFunctionAnalyses(MachineFunctionAnalysisManager &MFAM);\\n190: \\n191:   /// Construct the core LLVM function canonicalization and simplification\\n192:   /// pipeline.\\n193:   ///\\n194:   /// This is a long pipeline and uses most of the per-function optimization\\n195:   /// passes in LLVM to canonicalize and simplify the IR. It is suitable to run\\n196:   /// repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy important\\n197:   /// information about the semantics of the IR.\\n198:   ///\\n199:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n200:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n201:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n202:   /// build them.\\n203:   ///\\n204:   /// \\\\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\\n205:   LLVM_ABI FunctionPassManager buildFunctionSimplificationPipeline(\\n206:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n207: \\n208:   /// Construct the core LLVM module canonicalization and simplification\\n209:   /// pipeline.\\n210:   ///\\n211:   /// This pipeline focuses on canonicalizing and simplifying the entire module\\n212:   /// of IR. Much like the function simplification pipeline above, it is\\n213:   /// suitable to run repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy\\n214:   /// important information. It does, however, perform inlining and other\\n215:   /// heuristic based simplifications that are not strictly reversible.\\n216:   ///\\n217:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n218:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n219:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n220:   /// build them.\\n221:   ///\\n222:   /// \\\\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\\n223:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleSimplificationPipeline(\\n224:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n225: \\n226:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining as well as\\n227:   /// the inlining-driven cleanups.\\n228:   LLVM_ABI ModuleInlinerWrapperPass\\n229:   buildInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n230: \\n231:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining with\\n232:   /// module inliner pass.\\n233:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n234:   buildModuleInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n235: \\n236:   /// Construct the core LLVM module optimization pipeline.\\n237:   ///\\n238:   /// This pipeline focuses on optimizing the execution speed of the IR. It\\n239:   /// uses cost modeling and thresholds to balance code growth against runtime\\n240:   /// improvements. It includes vectorization and other information destroying\\n241:   /// transformations. It also cannot generally be run repeatedly on a module\\n242:   /// without potentially seriously regressing either runtime performance of\\n243:   /// the code or serious code size growth.\\n244:   ///\\n245:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n246:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n247:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n248:   /// build them.\\n249:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleOptimizationPipeline(\\n250:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase LTOPhase);\\n251: \\n252:   /// Build a per-module default optimization pipeline.\\n253:   ///\\n254:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for per-module\\n255:   /// optimization and code generation without any link-time optimization. It\\n256:   /// typically correspond to frontend \\\"-O[123]\\\" options for optimization\\n257:   /// levels \\\\c O1, \\\\c O2 and \\\\c O3 resp.\\n258:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline(\\n259:       OptimizationLevel Level,\\n260:       ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase = ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None);\\n261: \\n262:   /// Build a fat object default optimization pipeline.\\n263:   ///\\n264:   /// This builds a pipeline that runs the LTO/ThinLTO  pre-link pipeline, and\\n265:   /// emits a section containing the pre-link bitcode along side the object code\\n266:   /// generated in non-LTO compilation.\\n267:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildFatLTODefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\\n268:                                                         bool ThinLTO,\\n269:                                                         bool EmitSummary);\\n270: \\n271:   /// Build a pre-link, ThinLTO-targeting default optimization pipeline to\\n272:   /// a pass manager.\\n273:   ///\\n274:   /// This adds the pre-link optimizations tuned to prepare a module for\\n275:   /// a ThinLTO run. It works to minimize the IR which needs to be analyzed\\n276:   /// without making irreversible decisions which could be made better during\\n277:   /// the LTO run.\\n278:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n279:   buildThinLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level);\\n280: \\n281:   /// Build a ThinLTO default optimization pipeline to a pass manager.\\n282:   ///\\n283:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for link-time\\n284:   /// optimization and code generation. It is particularly tuned to fit well\\n285:   /// when IR coming into the LTO phase was first run through \\\\c\\n286:   /// buildThinLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline, and the two coordinate closely.\\n287:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildThinLTODefaultPipeline(\\n288:       OptimizationLevel Level, const ModuleSummaryIndex *ImportSummary);\\n289: \\n290:   /// Build a pre-link, LTO-targeting default optimization pipeline to a pass\\n291:   /// manager.\\n292:   ///\\n293:   /// This adds the pre-link optimizations tuned to work well with a later LTO\\n294:   /// run. It works to minimize the IR which needs to be analyzed without\\n295:   /// making irreversible decisions which could be made better during the LTO\\n296:   /// run.\\n297:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n298:   buildLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level);\\n299: \\n300:   /// Build an LTO default optimization pipeline to a pass manager.\\n301:   ///\\n302:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for link-time\\n303:   /// optimization and code generation. It is particularly tuned to fit well\\n304:   /// when IR coming into the LTO phase was first run through \\\\c\\n305:   /// buildLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline, and the two coordinate closely.\\n306:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildLTODefaultPipeline(\\n307:       OptimizationLevel Level, ModuleSummaryIndex *ExportSummary);\\n308: \\n309:   /// Build an O0 pipeline with the minimal semantically required passes.\\n310:   ///\\n311:   /// This should only be used for non-LTO and LTO pre-link pipelines.\\n312:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n313:   buildO0DefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\\n314:                          ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase = ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None);\\n315: \\n316:   /// Build the default `AAManager` with the default alias analysis pipeline\\n317:   /// registered.\\n318:   ///\\n319:   /// This also adds target-specific alias analyses registered via\\n320:   /// TargetMachine::registerDefaultAliasAnalyses().\\n321:   LLVM_ABI AAManager buildDefaultAAPipeline();\\n322: \\n323:   /// Parse a textual pass pipeline description into a \\\\c\\n324:   /// ModulePassManager.\\n325:   ///\\n326:   /// The format of the textual pass pipeline description looks something like:\\n327:   ///\\n328:   ///   module(function(instcombine,sroa),dce,cgscc(inliner,function(...)),...)\\n329:   ///\\n330:   /// Pass managers have ()s describing the nest structure of passes. All passes\\n331:   /// are comma separated. As a special shortcut, if the very first pass is not\\n332:   /// a module pass (as a module pass manager is), this will automatically form\\n333:   /// the shortest stack of pass managers that allow inserting that first pass.\\n334:   /// So, assuming function passes 'fpassN', CGSCC passes 'cgpassN', and loop\\n335:   /// passes 'lpassN', all of these are valid:\\n336:   ///\\n337:   ///   fpass1,fpass2,fpass3\\n338:   ///   cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3\\n339:   ///   lpass1,lpass2,lpass3\\n340:   ///\\n341:   /// And they are equivalent to the following (resp.):\\n342:   ///\\n343:   ///   module(function(fpass1,fpass2,fpass3))\\n344:   ///   module(cgscc(cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3))\\n345:   ///   module(function(loop(lpass1,lpass2,lpass3)))\\n346:   ///\\n347:   /// This shortcut is especially useful for debugging and testing small pass\\n348:   /// combinations.\\n349:   ///\\n350:   /// The sequence of passes aren't necessarily the exact same kind of pass.\\n351: public:\n43:   /// Constructor sets pipeline tuning defaults based on cl::opts. Each option\n44:   /// can be set in the PassBuilder when using a LLVM as a library.\n45:   LLVM_ABI PipelineTuningOptions();\n46: \n47:   /// Tuning option to set loop interleaving on/off, set based on opt level.\n48:   bool LoopInterleaving;\n49: \n50:   /// Tuning option to enable/disable loop vectorization, set based on opt\n51:   /// level.\n52:   bool LoopVectorization;\n53: \n54:   /// Tuning option to enable/disable slp loop vectorization, set based on opt\n55:   /// level.\n56:   bool SLPVectorization;\n57: \n58:   /// Tuning option to enable/disable loop unrolling. Its default value is\n88:   /// false.\n89:   bool MergeFunctions;\n90: \n91:   /// Tuning option to override the default inliner threshold.\n92:   int InlinerThreshold;\n93: \n94:   // Experimental option to eagerly invalidate more analyses. A name is either the name of a pass\n126:   /// (e.g. \"instcombine\") or the name of a pipeline type (e.g. \"cgscc\"). See parsePassPipeline() for a more\n129:   /// detailed description of the textual pipeline format.\n130:   struct PipelineElement {\n131:     StringRef Name;\n132:     std::vector<PipelineElement> InnerPipeline;\n133:   };\n134: \n135:   LLVM_ABI explicit PassBuilder(\n136:       TargetMachine *TM = nullptr,\n137:       PipelineTuningOptions PTO = PipelineTuningOptions(),\n138:       std::optional<PGOOptions> PGOOpt = std::nullopt,\n139:       PassInstrumentationCallbacks *PIC = nullptr,\n140:       IntrusiveRefCntPtr<vfs::FileSystem> FS = vfs::getRealFileSystem());\n141: \n142:   /// Cross register the analysis managers through their proxies.\n143:   ///\n144:   /// This is an interface that can be used to cross register each\n145:   /// AnalysisManager with all the others analysis managers.\n146:   LLVM_ABI void\n147:   crossRegisterProxies(LoopAnalysisManager &LAM, FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM,\n148:                        CGSCCAnalysisManager &CGAM, ModuleAnalysisManager &MAM,\n149:                        MachineFunctionAnalysisManager *MFAM = nullptr);\n150: \n151:   /// Registers all available module analysis passes.\n152:   ///\n153:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\c\n154:   /// ModuleAnalysisManager with all registered module analyses. Reason to run this late is that too\n1542:   // early versioning may prevent further inlining due to increase of code\n1543:   // size. Other optimizations which runs later might get benefit of no-alias\n1544:   // assumption in clone loop.\n1545:   if (UseLoopVersioningLICM) {\n1546:     OptimizePM.addPass(\n1547:         createFunctionToLoopPassAdaptor(LoopVersioningLICMPass()));\n1548:     // LoopVersioningLICM pass might increase new LICM opportunities.\n1549:     OptimizePM.addPass(createFunctionToLoopPassAdaptor(\n1550:         LICMPass(PTO.LicmMssaOptCap, PTO.LicmMssaNoAccForPromotionCap,\n1551:                  /*AllowSpeculation=*/true),\n1552:         /*USeMemorySSA=*/true));\n1553:   }\n1554: \n1555:   OptimizePM.addPass(Float2IntPass());\n1556:   OptimizePM.addPass(LowerConstantIntrinsicsPass());\n1557: \n1558:   if (EnableMatrix) {\n1559:     OptimizePM.addPass(LowerMatrixIntrinsicsPass());\n1560:     OptimizePM.addPass(EarlyCSEPass());\n1561:   }\n1562: \n1563:   // CHR pass should only be applied with the profile information.\n1564:   // The check is to check the profile summary information in CHR.\n1565:   if (EnableCHR && Level == OptimizationLevel::O3)\n1566:     OptimizePM.addPass(ControlHeightReductionPass());\n1567: \n1568:   // FIXME: We need to run some loop optimizations to re-rotate loops after\n1569:   // simplifycfg and others undo their rotation.\n1570: \n1571:   // Optimize the loop execution. These passes operate on entire loop nests\n1572:   // rather than on each loop in an inside-out manner, and so they are actually\n1573:   // function passes.\n1574: \n1575:   invokeVectorizerStartEPCallbacks(OptimizePM, Level);\n1576: \n1577:   LoopPassManager LPM;\n1578:   // First rotate loops that may have been un-rotated by prior passes.\n1579:   // Disable header duplication at -Oz.\n1580:   LPM.addPass(LoopRotatePass(EnableLoopHeaderDuplication ||\n1581:                                  Level != OptimizationLevel::Oz,\n1582:                              LTOPreLink));\n1583:   // Some loops may have become dead by now. Try to delete them.\n1584:   // FIXME: see discussion in https://reviews.llvm.org/D112851,\n1585:   //        this may need to be revisited once we run GVN before loop deletion\n1586:   //        in the simplification pipeline.\n1587:   LPM.addPass(LoopDeletionPass());\n1588: \n1589:   if (PTO.LoopInterchange)\n1590:     LPM.addPass(LoopInterchangePass());\n1591: \n1592:   OptimizePM.addPass(\n1593:       createFunctionToLoopPassAdaptor(std::move(LPM), /*UseMemorySSA=*/false));\n1594: \n1595:   // FIXME: This may not be the right place in the pipeline.\n1596:   // We need to have the data to support the right place.\n1597:   if (PTO.LoopFusion)\n1598:     OptimizePM.addPass(LoopFusePass());\n1599: \n1600:   // Distribute loops to allow partial vectorization.  I.e. isolate dependences\n1601:   // into separate loop that would otherwise inhibit vectorization.  This is\n1602:   // currently only performed for loops marked with the metadata\n1603:   // llvm.loop.distribute=true or when -enable-loop-distribute is specified.\n1604:   OptimizePM.addPass(LoopDistributePass());\n1605: \n1606:   // Populates the VFABI attribute with the scalar-to-vector mappings\n1607:   // from the TargetLibraryInfo.\n1608:   OptimizePM.addPass(InjectTLIMappings());\n1609: \n1610:   addVectorPasses(Level, OptimizePM, LTOPhase);\n1611: \n1612:   invokeVectorizerEndEPCallbacks(OptimizePM, Level);\n1613: \n1614:   // LoopSink pass sinks instructions hoisted by LICM, which serves as a\n1615:   // canonicalization pass that enables other optimizations. As a result,\n1616:   // LoopSink pass needs to be a very late IR pass to avoid undoing LICM\n1617:   // result too early.\n1618:   OptimizePM.addPass(LoopSinkPass());\n1619: \n1620:   // And finally clean up LCSSA form before generating code.\n1621:   OptimizePM.addPass(InstSimplifyPass());\n1622: \n1623:   // This hoists/decomposes div/rem ops. FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM =\n110:       AM.getResult<FunctionAnalysisManagerModuleProxy>(M).getManager();\n111: \n112:   // Request PassInstrumentation from analysis manager, will use it to run\n113:   // instrumenting callbacks for the passes later.\n114:   PassInstrumentation PI = AM.getResult<PassInstrumentationAnalysis>(M);\n115: \n116:   PreservedAnalyses PA = PreservedAnalyses::all();\n117:   for (Function &F : M) {\n118:     if (F.isDeclaration())\n119:       continue;\n120: \n121:     // Check the PassInstrumentation's BeforePass callbacks before running the\n122:     // pass, skip its execution completely if asked to (callback returns\n123:     // false).\n124:     if (!PI.runBeforePass<Function>(*Pass, F))\n125:       continue;\n126: \n127:     PreservedAnalyses PassPA = Pass->run(F, FAM);\n128: \n129:     // We know that the function pass couldn't have invalidated any other\n130:     // function's analyses (that's the contract of a function pass), so\n131:     // directly handle the function analysis manager's invalidation here.\n132:     FAM.invalidate(F, EagerlyInvalidate ? PreservedAnalyses::none() : PassPA);\n133: \n134:     PI.runAfterPass(*Pass, F, PassPA);\n135: \n136:     // Then intersect the preserved set so that invalidation of module\n137:     // analyses will eventually occur when the module pass completes.\n138:     PA.intersect(std::move(PassPA));\n139:   }\n140: \n141:   // The FunctionAnalysisManagerModuleProxy is preserved because (we assume)\n142:   // the function passes we ran didn't add or remove any functions.\n143:   //\n144:   // We also preserve all analyses on Functions, because we did all the\n145:   // invalidation we needed to do above.\n146:   PA.preserveSet<AllAnalysesOn<Function>>();\n147:   PA.preserve<FunctionAnalysisManagerModuleProxy>();\n148:   return PA;\n149: }\n150: \n151: template <>\n152: void llvm::printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\n153:                                                 const Module &IR) {\n154:   OS << \"module \\\"\" << IR.getName() << \"\\\"\";\n155: }\n156: \n157: template <>\n158: void llvm::printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\n159:                                                   const Function &IR) {\n160:   OS << \"function \\\"\" << IR.getName() << \"\\\"\";\n161: }\n162: \n163: AnalysisSetKey CFGAnalyses::SetKey;\n164: \n165: AnalysisSetKey PreservedAnalyses::AllAnalysesKey;\n166: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/lib/IR/PassManager.cpp"}}}

Chain\\n\\n### Overview\\nLLVM uses a sophisticated pass infrastructure with two systems: the Legacy PassManager and the New PassManager. The New PassManager uses modern C++ template-based design with concept-based polymorphism.\\n\\n### PassManager Template (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h)\\nThe core PassManager is a template class that manages sequences of passes over IR units (Modules, Functions, Loops, etc.). Key features:\\n- Template parameters: IRUnitT (e.g., Module, Function), AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs\\n- Specializations for ModulePassManager and FunctionPassManager (lines 238, 247)\\n- Uses `addPass()` template method (lines 193-214) which uses concept-based polymorphism\\n- Each pass is wrapped in a PassModel that implements the PassConcept interface\\n- Executes passes via the `run()` method which:\\n  1. Iterates through stored passes\\n  2. Calls each pass's run() method with the IR unit\\n  3. Updates analysis results based on PreservedAnalyses returned by each pass\\n\\n### PassRegistry (llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h and llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp)\\nProvides global registration and lookup for passes:\\n- PassRegistry::getPassRegistry() returns the singleton global registry (PassRegistry.cpp:23-26)\\n- Stores PassInfo objects in two maps: by type ID and by string name (PassRegistry.h:42-46)\\n- registerPass() method adds PassInfo to both maps (PassRegistry.cpp:48-62)\\n- Used by legacy PassManager for dependency resolution\\n- Thread-unsafe by design - each thread needs its own registry\\n\\n### PassInfo (llvm/include/llvm/PassInfo.h)\\nMetadata class for passes containing:\\n- Pass name and command-line argument (lines 34-35)\\n- Pass ID pointer (type identifier) (line 36)\\n- Function pointer to pass constructor (line 39)\\n- Flags indicating analysis/CFG-only status (lines 37-38)\\n- Used primarily by legacy passes but referenced in modern infrastructure\\n\\n### PassBuilder (llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h)\\nThe main class for constructing standard optimization pipelines:\\n- Holds TargetMachine, PipelineTuningOptions, PGOOptions\\n- Core pipeline building methods:\\n  - buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline() - per-module default pipeline for O1/O2/O3 (line 258)\\n  - buildModuleSimplificationPipeline() - canonicalization and simplification passes (line 223)\\n  - buildModuleOptimizationPipeline() - speed optimization passes (line 249)\\n  - buildInlinerPipeline() - inlining passes (line 228)\\n  - buildFunctionSimplificationPipeline() - per-function simplification (line 205)\\n\\n### Standard Optimization Pipeline (llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp)\\nImplements the actual pipeline construction for O2/O3 optimization levels:\\n\\n**buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline (lines 1715-1761)**:\\n1. Returns O0 pipeline for O0 level\\n2. Adds memory profiling cleanup if non-LTO\\n3. Adds annotation to metadata conversion\\n4. Adds force function attributes\\n5. Calls buildModuleSimplificationPipeline (line 1746)\\n6. Calls buildModuleOptimizationPipeline (line 1749)\\n7. Adds LTO pre-link passes if applicable\\n\\n**buildModuleOptimizationPipeline (lines 1477-1651)**:\\nThis is the O2/O3 optimization pipeline that includes:\\n1. Partial inlining (line 1486)\\n2. Reverse post-order function attribute inference (line 1503)\\n3. PGO instrumentation passes (lines 1509-1517)\\n4. Recompute GlobalsAA (line 1528)\\n5. Function-level optimization PM (OptimizePM):\\n   - Loop optimization: LoopRotatePass, LoopDeletionPass, LoopInterchangePass (lines 1580-1590)\\n   - Loop distribution (line 1604)\\n   - Vector passes (line 1610)\\n   - LoopSinkPass (line 1618)\\n   - InstSimplifyPass (line 1621)\\n   - DivRemPairsPass (line 1626)\\n   - TailCallElimPass (line 1630)\\n   - SimplifyCFGPass (line 1635)\\n6. Module-level optimization via ModuleToFunctionPassAdaptor (line 1642)\\n7. AllocTokenPass if non-LTO (line 1648)\\n\\n### Pass Registry Definitions (llvm/lib/Passes/PassRegistry.def)\\nMacro-based registry that defines all available passes:\\n- MODULE_ANALYSIS: Module-level analyses (CallGraph, DXILMetadata, etc.)\\n- MODULE_PASS: Module passes (AlwaysInliner, Annotation2Metadata, Attributor, etc.)\\n- CGSCC_PASS: Call graph SCC passes\\n- FUNCTION_PASS: Function passes\\n- LOOP_PASS: Loop passes\\n- Each pass definition allows the pass to be constructed via PassBuilder and named in command-line interfaces\\n\\n### Pass Execution Flow (llvm/lib/IR/PassManager.cpp)\\nWhen PassManager::run() is called:\\n1. For each registered pass (line 225 - Passes vector)\\n2. Retrieves PreservedAnalyses from previous pass\\n3. Calls pass's run() method with IR unit and AnalysisManager\\n4.
